< Text>
The Cockatoo was very pleased with incoming customers.  11/10 recommend.  Also Tony is awesome. I was sick and tired off all the fillers in pet food,  went to Tony's shop who has a 17 and 15 year old shop cats with no liver disease and healthy kidneys. I asked him what food he feeds them and my cat LOVES it. Her coat is shiny and she looks forward to meal times,  she's no longer hunting as much to make up for the vitamins her Pet Co and Pet Smart food didn't have.  He sells the stuff wayyyyy cheaper than Daryel's pet shop in Redlands (Red Barn Naturals and Taste of the wild). Tony also explained that he only sells his food at a 25% markup to make it affordable for customers.  Yucipa is really out of the way for me but I'll drive 30 minutes to buy from his shop any time I need to restock. He also sells flea medication and worm pills by the pill/ cartridge if you can't afford to drop $45 or $30 on a couple months supply.</Text>

<review>It's artisanal ice cream, and overpriced. Yes, the flavors are good, the ice cream and sorbets are extremely smooth, like a perfectly defrosted tub of ice cream, and the presentation is great. But, you're paying a premium for this ice cream. This wouldn't be so bad, except that the actual serving sizes they provide are disappointingly small. A single scoop of ice cream will cost you as much a tub of premium ice cream from the store. Two scoops is going to cost you nearly $10.

Service was also quite slow despite there being only 4 people total ordering in the store when I visited around 7:30pm. Can't imagine what the wait would be like mid day in the summer.

Otherwise, it's a cool atmosphere. Well designed, lots of sitting room inside and out. It's a decent date location.

TL;DR: Good, tasty ice cream at a high price, in a modern environment. Small portions compared to other ice cream stores. Would recommend going once just to try it.<//review><Time>1530093810928<//Time>< Pictures>

<Review>Over the past 5 months, HSC has become "my gym". I feel like part of a not-so-little family here where everybody fist bumps you to say hi and people yell out your name excitedly when you walk in the door. My own family doesn't even get that excited to see me.

Comparing my experience here to tons of studios and commercial gyms I've been to, staff + members + events = amazing community.

STAFF
Austin (the owner) teaches some mean cardio and boxing classes to get you in shape where I almost passed out the first time I went. Ivy will kick your butt in a$$ class and then spend time helping you individually to correct your pull-up form. Kim does all things powerlifting and will hold you to the highest standard as she cheers you on when you bench more than you thought you could. Tim does all things Olympic weightlifting and super patiently tells you time and time again how you need to stop holding the barbell like you're about to mic drop. Myra is the in-house physical therapist and does a weekly stretching class that helps your muscles release through a series of challenging movements (no laying around here!). Plus Arthur, Jessie, Kolin, and the rest of the staff who do an amazing job supporting members and making sure HSC is running smoothly.

All of this matters because I've been to studios where I got yelled at for not following/understanding the instructor's direction. (Thankfully, Tim never yells at me for misreading BTN as "below the knee" and not "below the neck".  -_- ) If you're serious about improving in something, a coach will help put together a customized plan for you. There's even a Facebook group where the coaches do weekly check-ins!

MEMBERS
People actually made an effort to introduce themselves and say hi. I progressed in large part to both getting help and tips from other members and being inspired by watching the gains that everyone else was making. Knowing that I'll be seeing the same set of people 3x a week makes me feel accountable in actually showing up to the gym consistently.

EVENTS
There was an Olympic lifting meet in East Bay recently, and it was awesome to see so many members of the gym show up to support other members who had been training for months to compete for the first time. HSC even held a mock powerlifting meet to help beginners feel good about competing! On top of just meets, HSC hosts holiday parties and tons of social events throughout the year.

A friend tried to convince me to join Equinox (hello, Eucalyptus towels!), but when I went, nobody was there to correct my form or made sure I knew what I was doing. Nobody was chatting between sets about random stuff like the best way to tie up long hair. At the end of the day, no amount of Kiehl's products can replace the community here.</Review>< Pictures>

Having met the head coach/gym owner Austin before HSC, I came into the gym when it started, hoping for the best. I had known him to be an amazing conditioning coach and he was the one who fostered my love of powerlifting.

The gym is nearing its second year in a couple months and I can truly say my expectations have been completely blown out of the water. On the powerlifting side, I have had several coaches mentor me at HSC. I've watched my lift totals rise higher and higher. On the conditioning side, I've had coaches teach me to love the intensity of it all. Conditioning classes are never boring and I've always felt challenged.

Classes aside, what I find to be the best quality of this gym is the community. In every class, there's a sense of camaraderie. We cheer each other on through each set or each lap. When I'm tired and want to sleep after a long work day and commute, knowing that I have a group of friends and coaches at the gym helps motivate me to come in.

So if you're looking for a gym full of qualified trainers to help you reach your goals and members to cheer you on and work out alongside you, come check out HSC!!</review>

< Text>
We were able to get in for a last minute birthday dinner. Service was very friendly.
Appetizer - calamari and also the polenta with mushrooms were both good and satisfying for a table.
Dinner - Pasta dishes were excellent. Lamb, filet, and veal parmigiana were also very good. Salmon piccata was just okay (needed more sauce/capers and only a few veggies included).
Dessert - Tiramisu was outstanding, but the  chocolate lava cake had a solid center and the flourless chocolate cake was a brick.
A few items requested never arrived (milk for child and coffee came after dessert). Over all would return for a date night, but not a party over 4.< /Text>

<rate>1</rate>< text>
Stopped by this afternoon and ordered two drinks: a hot tea and an iced coffee. The store was not busy, but with only two people working the service was  extremely slow. The iced coffee came immediately, but I waited for the tea for  over 15 minutes. I  had to ask  the whereabouts of my drink because many other customers with more complex drinks were entering, ordering (not online orders), and exiting with their drinks before me. The person making the drinks ignored  me when I asked twice. This person was VERY busy (the only one actually making all the drinks) and I could see how hard they were working, so I asked the person at the register. Their attitude was not welcoming and even seemed annoyed that I asked after patiently waiting. I told this person that they need more people working. I was not trying to be rude- just stating the obvious, but this person's response was full of much attitude and eye rolls. They proceeded to tell me that they were sick with food poisoning from the night before and at least they came into work. I asked if there was a manager I could contact and they would not give me a name. I asked if there was a number I could call to complain and they literally said, "call whoever you want, I don't care".  It's unfortunate that me as a paying customer receives treatment like this. I can see if I was rude to the employee, but I was not rude or disrespectful....I am disappointed with this location, and this is not the first time. This Starbucks is always so understaffed- with waiting times of over 15 minutes for simple drinks. Writing a negative review online is is not a common occurrence for me, but I am repeatedly dissatisfied with the service.

Hopefully management can staff more effectively. It might decrease employee stress on the job.<//text>

<Text>I need to start by saying I've visited Homewood once a year for the past 2 or 3 years and loved it. This time, however, it wasn't the best, although still good. The staff were nice as usual,  although I had rather few interactions. My biggest complaint was the lack of value compared to the other big resorts in the area. The cost is about the same as the other places, but there are not features to match. They even charged to park as well as for the RFID cards they use now for lift tickets. They only have one high speed lift, and it's not the first one you get on. The first one was painfully slow. There is only one restroom up on the mountain even though there is a lot of terrain. So, not my favorite experience this time, but gorgeous views! Look, if there's snow at Lake Tahoe, then do yourself a favor and skip the lines at Squaw and go to Homewood Mountain Resort. Bring the family and enjoy the small-time atmosphere. <Rating>4<//Rating>< review>
We've been here twice this year since the season start. My son and I took ski lesson. Kid ski class are separate from the main area  it a little down south in Tahoe bowl there are shittle bus run to both place every 5 minutes. My kid loves his teacher Gretchen has been very kind to him and encourages him to jeep on skiing. The whole day lesson cost $165 including Lunch and snack from 9am to 3:30pm I'd recommend to book them in advance.

Adult ski lesson is $65 if you book in advance plus rental gear 10 am - 12:30 pm I took lessons with Ramsay and Cindy they were both such great teacher.

Overall we enjoy coming to Homewood so much basically base on the price and uncrowded especially in the week.</review>

I really enjoyed my time at home wood. However despite the amazing views I don't think this is the place I would recommend teaching someone new.

Apart from the magic carpet the only other "lift" that was offered on the lesson + lift pass + rebtal was 1 janky T bar that was not well groomed that I sat and watched more than 50% of new skiers and boarders fall off for 15 minutes.

We luckily had a second day booked that was just lift tickets + rental which allowed us to go to the top of the mountain where we had a lot of fun and a good drink at the bar.

I must however give this place 2 stars as I find it highly deceptive to sell a 'lift pass' that does not include any lifts.< /review>

<text>Fun place to visit and brilliantly priced for lift tickets, rentals, and lessons. There were plenty of options for any skill level of skier or snowboarder. The park was well maintained and the map was fairly easy to read. If you book online in advance you can get some really great deals.

However, I had some gift cards and wanted to use them to book online  but there is no option to use them in the checkout. I called several times and the phone was never answered.  I called the order helpline and the woman couldn't figure out how to do it either. She also called the resort and got no answer. I did eventually get a call back but it was 10 minutes before they closed and I was at work and couldn't answer.

The lessons were cheap but rather short on time and some seemed better than others. The instructors were very friendly but all seem to work at different paces. One group would advance rather quickly and thoroughly, making sure the students could perform the maneuvers with some accuracy. While others seemed to rush through the steps and pushed forward regardless of whether the students were ready. So I think there needs to be some consistency between the instructors and perhaps a lesson curriculum for the lessons.

Overall it was a great time and I will definitely be visiting Homewood again. I would recommend this place for beginners through advanced skiers and riders and for people of all ages.</text><Date>1546977700590</Date>< Rating>

<date>1579583544219< /date><Rating>2</Rating><Review>I'm on the fence about Homewood, it's a great resort for beginners and learners in my opinion as it has great greens and blue runs to learn and practice your techniques but for slightly more advanced skier's it is terrible, the lifts are slow and the blacks are either the equivalent of a hard blue or an ungroomed hard blue and they provide little challenge. I also call into question the quality of the maintenance that they perform as the most important chair (Ellis) was shut down for half a day because it couldn't handle the weight of a full load of people riding up to the top, that isn't just maintenance, not being able to complete its only objetive is a design flaw. The safety is also an issue as half of the lifts lack a safety bar and creak as they make their ascent. Additionally, as a result of the lack of safety Ellis and Madden are incredibly slow. Ellis was also stationary with riders on it for over 30 min  before they got let the riders off of the lift while I was there. The other issue I found with the resort was the fact that some runs were marked as blacks on the map but when arriving at the runs, they were marked as blues (ex. Jimmy's Run). That being said, the lake views were amazing and the pictures you see will not due it justice.< /Review>< pictures>

Due to the season, most routes are icy, and I realize that the resort can not control the weather.

However, one thing that can be changed is the organization. Unlike other resorts such as Northstar, Homewood poorly organizes ski lift lines. This resulted in a bunch of delays, plus a lot of minor injuries.

Also, grooming could be improved. I‚Äôm no double black skier, but I can tell the difference between good and bad routes. Again, some things you can‚Äôt control. Perhaps the crowds ruin it too quickly.

But overall, still worth the visit! Just be aware this isn‚Äôt the best of the best< /text>

< Name>
Steve Mattos (#SteveInRealLife)</Name>
<rate>4< /rate><Response>None< /Response><UserId.>116207775664068765339< /UserId.>< review>
If you're reading these reviews, ignore 99% of the complaints. As a LONG TIME ski resort insider, everything that goes on at Homewood from non-transferable tickets to "the scary meter ledge" in the beginner area is all perfectly normal. I live on the other side of the lake and I've always enjoyed an occasional trip around to hit up Homewood in a good season. If you're a beginner, the easy runs are going to seem a little more intermediate than you might like. If you're an expert, unless Quail is open, you're going to be a little disappointed with the groomers but the trees at Homewood are super fun with adequate coverage. Homewood is a very basic mountain, though they're planning a great deal of upgrades. Homewood has been a long time local-knowledge mountain and even with the planned expansion, it might be safer for totally inexperienced skiers bringing the whole family up to Tahoe from...oh I don't know...let's say San Jose - to go ahead and save their patronage for the I-80 boiler plate resorts. Whether you're local or a vacationer, though, if you're more interested in skiing than shopping and you're looking for a mainly intermediate hill, Homewood's the place. You'll also be hard pressed to find better views of Tahoe at any other resort.

Ignore the negative reviews. They're either from people who have little to no experience skiing or people who are used to being catered to non-stop. Tahoe is not Vail and we never will be. We're here to cater to people who love their respective sports and we do it exceptionally well everywhere in the Tahoe Basin.< /review>

I searched all over South Lake Tahoe for ski and snow boarding lessons, for my 4 nieces and 4 nephews.  This was their first time in the snow. This 5 star review is based on our ski team experience at Homewood.

For anyone who is looking for a ski team for his/her child, this is the place to be. The coaches Deedee, Josh and Jenefer are positive, engaged and enthused. They are professional and work well with all parents and children.  They take the time to make the team fun and at the same time, teach each child new skills.  They take the time to follow up with parents before and after each session.  They go beyond "oh, we had a good time today" or "your child did well."  They make sure the parents get to know one another. Kids of all ages have become friends with one another.  This has truly become a mini-community. Everyone involved is extremely welcoming.  There are no egos.

We hope Homewood recognizes the coaches' professional expertise and experience.  At times, we do wonder if there is recognition on how much the coaches offer to this program.  With their years of experiences, Deedee, Josh and Jen could probably coach at  a larger resort; we feel so fortunate they are at Homewood.  One can easily tell they love what they do and they are good at what they do.  We hope Homewood recognizes their level of experience and parents' levels of gratitude.</Review>

<review>I would not recommend Homewood for a beginner due to the lack of terrain that is easily accessible from the lifts.  For an intermediate, the resort is great.  It is less crowded and offers some great opportunities to maximize your ski time.  The biggest downside is that most of their lifts have not been upgraded and are pretty slow, and there aren't that many lifts on the mountain.  The mid-mountain "lodge" is really a very large tent that provides good shelter and packaged food (they grill outside on sunny days). Bathrooms are outside which requires a bit of a hike down an incline and up some stairs.  It's a family resort with reasonable prices and friendly people, so don't expect 5 star accommodations, but what they have in place is adequate if you aren't a snob.<//review>< pics>

As a beginner snowboarder who only goes once a year, Homewood is very easy to access and affordable! You don't have to drive up any windy mountain roads or trek a mile to the ski lift. You can see the mountain from the road. Parking is easy and the ski lift is close to the main cabin.

I would definitely return. Although I would recommend renting equipment elsewhere, since it was quite pricy. I only needed a helmet for a day, and it cost me $29.<//text>

<GmapID>0x80997fda4762005f:0x73b0c46aa0c1068d< /GmapID><text>Runs are not well connected. But great views of the lake!!<//text><userid>103757448775143321160</userid></record></dataset><record>
<Review>It truly amazes me why people are skiing Northstar or Heavenly and overlooking Tahoe Gems like Homewood. This place is rife with Tahoe Magic. Best views of the lake, PERIOD. Tree runs for daze! Freshies a week after a storm. Along the crest, so they always get big dumps. Quail face is steeper than all of Northstar. A relic of Tahoe's past- back in the day when a family ski vacation was pulling up, throwing skis on the kids, bringing a sac lunch, drinking beer with the staff in the lodge, and cheap lift tickets. Yes, they dont have 5 star accomodations at the base, or a f*ing ice rink, or overpriced drinks at a bourgeois cocktail bar, and thats a good thing. Get back to the soul of skiing, and homewood is where you do it. Tell your friends, cause we need to keep this place in business...< /Review><date>1481503443168<//date>< gmap_id>
0x80997fda4762005f:0x73b0c46aa0c1068d</gmap_id>
<response>None<//response>< user_id>
112964973303968124592</user_id>
< rating>
5<//rating>
< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>
< Name>
Jay Weaver<//Name>
</record>
</dataset><record>
< text>
The experience was great!

I visited Homewood on 12/30/2015 with my brother and another family friend. After arriving at about 11:00 a.m., we parked at the main parking lot which was conviniently located at the base of the slopes. Parking was short, but additional street parking was offered. Within five minutes, we had bought out lift tickets. Unlike Boreal, the crowd was managed very well - the crowds were same as Boreal but no lines were present.

After ten minutes, we joined the bunny slope line in order to warm up. One bad thing about Homewood is that the bunny slope lifts are simply poles hanging from a cable which you have to hang on to. They are slow, single rider at a time, and difficult to use. We then went to the Madden triple chair, which was unfortunately a Yan lift. These lifts are unimaginably slow, hard to board, and have no safety bar. This lift was slightly faster and much easier to board than other Yan lifts, but the ride to mid-mountain took about 9 minutes.

We skied for hours riding the advanced blue slopes and trying out the terrain park. The view was excellent, and the trails were groomed very well. The resort had an excellent mountain, with a bunny slope coming all the way from the summit to the base. Blues of different levels covered a large portion of the 1200 acres, many of which provided as a transition from green to blue and blue to black. Double black diamonds were also located at Homewood, offering a great view of the lake.

We rode the Old Homewood Express, which was the best express chairlift I had gone on. Within 4.5 minutes, we were at the summit. The blue slopes were perfect, with a right mix of packed powder and loose powder.

The Ore Car trail, which serves as a connection from the mountain to the North Lodge, was narrow, icy, and neglected. The sign pointing to the trail had fallen down, and a long uphill stretch was required in order to reach the slope. If you want to ski from top to base and do not want to ski on a black diamond, take the Lombard Street Slope. Unfortunately, you cannot ski at high speed down a small section of this winding slope, but it is an excellent slope for all levels, as it is wide and groomed very well.

Overall, Homewood was a great resort offering views of the lake, excellent powder, and a large variety of trails. I also liked the ski school and the cafeteria. Homewood is an everyone's resort, with trails ranging from beginner to expert. Visitors and non-skiers can walk all the way up the bunny slope and give instruction to their kids. I think Homewood is the best family resort I have been to. I suggest that if you want to go skiing and are any level below extreme expert, Homewood is the place for you.</text>
